## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt (population growth rate) as a function of time t and population size P, which is the canonical setup for continuous-time ecological growth models and their extensions (density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting, and seasonal/time-varying environments).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita growth rate)
- Exponential with time-varying rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slowly changing environment causing linear trend in per-capita rate)
- Immigration–emigration (linear): dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (net constant inflow/outflow plus proportional growth/decline)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; simplest self-limitation)
- Higher-order density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (stronger crowding or multiple limiting mechanisms)
- Gompertz-type growth (log density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (per-capita growth declines with log size; asymmetric approach to saturation)
- Theta-logistic / Richards-type: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible crowding shape; c2 controls curvature of density dependence)
- Allee effect (strong) cubic form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P, positive at intermediate P, negative at high P)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (removal rate proportional to population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (fixed quota harvesting; risk of collapse at low P)
- Saturating (Holling type II) harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P / (P + c2) (removal saturates at high P due to effort/handling limits)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (periodic environment modulating per-capita growth with density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If per-capita growth dP_dt/P is approximately constant across P, expect dP_dt proportional to P (linear in P).
- If growth slows smoothly as P increases and approaches a carrying capacity, expect a negative quadratic term (−P**2) or a factor like P*(1−const*P).
- If there is evidence of multiple equilibria (growth rate crosses zero at several P values), polynomial factorizations like P*(a*P−1)*(1−b*P) are natural.
- If small populations tend to decline (positive density dependence at low P), include an Allee factor (a*P−1) multiplying P.
- If environmental effects are periodic in time, parameters multiplying P (or the crowding term) often include sin(c*t+c).
- If environment quality trends over time (e.g., gradual deterioration/improvement), use slowly varying coefficients such as (c0+c1*t) or exp(c0+c1*t) multiplying P.
- If there is a baseline external input/output (stocking, migration, constant removal), add an additive constant term in dP_dt (±c0).
- If removal/harvesting saturates at high P, use a rational term in P such as P/(P+c) to cap the magnitude of the removal rate.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG2)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)= (0.2569297861)\,P\sin(0.7218439643\,t)\;+\;(0.1149290460)\,P e^{-0.03038461977\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be **exactly linear in \(P\)** (no constant-in-\(P\) terms, no \(\log(P\cdot)\), no \(P^\alpha\) with \(\alpha\neq 1\), no rational \(P/(P+c)\), etc.), and must contain **exactly** a \(P\sin(\omega t)\) term plus a \(P e^{kt}\) term (with \(k<0\)), with no extra \(t\)-only terms.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether its extra structures can be eliminated by setting parameters to 0 and whether the remaining form can be made identical to GT for all \(t,P\).

---

### 1.
Has additive \(c3\) (constant), a \(\log(c5 e^{c6 t}+1)\) term (depends on \(t\) but not \(P\)), and an \(e^{c8 t}\log(Pc9+1)\) term (nonlinear in \(P\)). You can zero some coefficients, but then you lose the required \(P e^{kt}\) term (there is no plain \(P e^{kt}\) term available). Not match.

### 2.
Contains \(\log(Pc4+1)\) and \(e^{c6 t}\log(Pc7+1)\): nonlinear in \(P\). If you set those coefficients to 0, you only keep \(P\sin(\cdot)\) and lose the exponential-in-\(t\) linear-in-\(P\) term. Not match.

### 3.
Has \(P^{1/5}c0\) (wrong \(P\)-dependence), constant \(c4\), and \(e^{c6 t}\log(Pc7+1)\) (nonlinear). Cannot become exactly GT. Not match.

### 4.
Has \(P c3/(P+c4)\) (not linear in \(P\) for all \(P\) unless \(c3=0\)), constant \(c5\), and \(e^{c7 t}\log(Pc8+1)\) (nonlinear). No way to produce \(P e^{kt}\) term. Not match.

### 5.
Has \(P c3\log(Pc4+1)\) (nonlinear in \(P\)) and \(e^{c7 t}\log(Pc8+1)\) (nonlinear). If removed, no \(P e^{kt}\). Not match.

### 6.
Form: \(P c0\sin(c1+c2 t) + c3 + c4 e^{c5 t}\log(Pc6+1)\).
The exponential part is tied to \(\log(Pc6+1)\) (nonlinear). Setting \(c4=0\) removes it, leaving no \(P e^{kt}\). Also constant \(c3\) must be 0 but then still missing exponential term. Not match.

### 7.
Has \(P^{1/5}c0\), \(P c4/(P+c5)\) (nonlinear), constant \(c6\), and \(e^{c8 t}\log(Pc9+1)\) (nonlinear). Not match.

### 8.
Has \(\log(c4 (P c5)^{c6}+1)\) (nonlinear in \(P\)) and \(e^{c8 t}\log(Pc9+1)\) (nonlinear). No plain \(P e^{kt}\). Not match.

### 9.
Has \(P^{c3}c4\) (unless \(c3=1\) becomes linear, but then it is just \(c4 P\), not \(P e^{kt}\)), plus \(e^{c6 t}\log(Pc7+1)\) (nonlinear). Not match.

### 10.
Has \(P^{1/5}c0\), plus a linear \(P c4\) and constant \(c5\), and \(e^{c7 t}\log(Pc8+1)\) (nonlinear). Not match.

### 11.
Has extra \(c3 e^{c4 t}\sin(c5+c6 t)\) term **not multiplied by \(P\)**; GT has no \(P\)-independent \(t\)-term. Only way is set \(c3=0\). Then remaining \(e^{c8 t}\log(Pc9+1)\) is nonlinear; setting \(c7=0\) leaves only \(P\sin\), missing \(P e^{kt}\). Not match.

### 12.
Second term is \(P c3 \sin(c4\log(c5 e^{c6 t}+1)+c7)\), not an exponential \(P e^{kt}\). No parameter choice makes \(\sin(\text{log-exp})\) equal \(e^{kt}\) for all \(t\). Not match.

### 13.
Second term \(P c3 \log(c4 e^{c5 t}+1)\) is not proportional to \(e^{kt}\) for all \(t\) (log of affine-in-exp). Cannot equal \(P e^{kt}\) identically. Not match.

### 14.
Has \(P c0\) and \(P c4\) (extra linear-in-\(P\) constants) and \(P c5\log(c6 e^{c7 t}+1)\) (not exponential). You could set \(c0=c4=0\), but the log term cannot become \(P e^{kt}\). Not match.

### 15.
Only \(P\sin(\cdot)\) plus \(P c3 e^{c4 t}\sin(c5+c6 t)\). The second factor is exponential times sine; to become pure exponential, you’d need \(\sin(c5+c6 t)\) constant for all \(t\), so set \(c6=0\), giving \(\sin(c5)\) constant. Then term becomes \(P (c3\sin c5) e^{c4 t}\), which matches GT’s exponential term by choosing:
- \(c4=-0.03038461977\)
- \(c3\sin(c5)=0.1149290460\)
And the first sine term must match \(0.2569297861 P\sin(0.7218439643 t)\). Candidate has \(\sin(c1+c2 t)\); set phase \(c1=0\) (or any \(2\pi k\)) and \(c2=0.7218439643\), \(c0=0.2569297861\).
This works. **Match possible.**

### 16.
\(P c0\sin(c1+c2 t) + P c3 e^{c4 t}\). This is exactly the GT structure (phase shift allowed). Set:
- \(c1=0\) (mod \(2\pi\))
- \(c2=0.7218439643\)
- \(c0=0.2569297861\)
- \(c4=-0.03038461977\)
- \(c3=0.1149290460\)
**Match possible.**

### 17.
Has extra \(P c0\) and \(P c4\) and an exponential*sine term. You could set \(c0=c4=0\). Then exponential*sine must reduce to pure exponential: set its sine argument constant by making coefficient of \(t\) zero (here \(\sin(c7 t + c8)\): set \(c7=0\)), giving constant \(\sin(c8)\). Then term becomes \(P(c5\sin c8)e^{c6 t}\), which can match GT exponential. Also set the main sine phase \(c2=0\) and \(c3=0.7218439643\) etc. So **match possible**.

### 18.
Contains \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) (can set \(c3=1\) to get \(P c4 e^{c5 t}\)), but also has \(c6\log(Pc7+1)\) (nonlinear in \(P\)) which must be removed by \(c6=0\). Then it becomes \(P\sin(\cdot)+P e^{\cdot}\) and can match. **Match possible.**

### 19.
Has \(P^{1/5}c0\) and constant \(c8\) and an exponential*sine term. You can set \(c0=0\), \(c8=0\), and reduce exponential*sine to pure exponential by setting its sine frequency zero (\(c6=0\)) so \(\sin(c7)\) constant, yielding \(P(c4\sin c7)e^{c5 t}\). Then match GT. **Match possible.**

### 20.
Has \(P^{1/5}c0\) and \(P^{c4}c5 e^{c6 t}\). Set \(c0=0\), \(c4=1\) to get \(P c5 e^{c6 t}\), and set \(c7=0\). Then match sine term and exponential term. **Match possible.**

### 21.
\(P\sin(\cdot)+P c3 e^{c4 t}+c5\). Need \(c5=0\). Then identical structure to GT. **Match possible.**

### 22.
Has \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) (can set \(c3=1\)) but also an extra \(c6\sin(c7\log(c8 t+1)+c9)\) term independent of \(P\); must set \(c6=0\). Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 23.
Has \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) (set \(c3=1\)) plus constant \(c6\) and a product \(\log(Pc8+1)\log(c9 t+1)\) (nonlinear in \(P\) and \(t\)). Must set \(c7=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 24.
Has \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) (set \(c3=1\)) plus constant \(c6\) and \(\log(Pc8+1)\) (nonlinear). Set \(c7=0\), \(c6=0\). Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 25.
Has \(P c3\log(Pc4+1)\) (nonlinear) and exponential*sine term plus constant \(c9\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c9=0\). Reduce exponential*sine to pure exponential by setting \(c7=0\) so \(\sin(c8)\) constant. Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 26.
Has \(P c3\) and \(P^{c4}c5 e^{c6 t}\) and constant \(c7\). Need no extra \(P\) constant term: set \(c3=0\). Set \(c4=1\) to make exponential term linear in \(P\). Set \(c7=0\). Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 27.
Has extra \(P c3\) and constant \(c6\). Set \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\). Then \(P c4 e^{c5 t}\) provides exponential term; match parameters. **Match possible.**

### 28.
Has extra \(P c0\), \(P c4\), constant \(c9\), and exponential*sine with phase \(c7+c8 t\). Set \(c0=c4=c9=0\). Set \(c8=0\) so sine constant \(\sin(c7)\), giving pure exponential. Then matches. **Match possible.**

### 29.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)**

where c0=0.2569, c1=0.7218, c2=0.1149, c3=0.03038.

Key observations about GT:
- It's a sum of two terms, both linear in P
- First term: P*sin(c1*t) — a sinusoidal oscillation in t, scaled by P
- Second term: P*exp(-c3*t) — an exponential decay in t, scaled by P
- No constant offset (no terms independent of P)
- No log terms, no P^(1/5) terms, no P/(P+c) terms

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Candidate 16: P*c0*sin(c1 + c2*t) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)**

This is P*c0*sin(c1+c2*t) + P*c3*exp(c4*t). Setting c1=0 (phase shift), c2=0.7218, c0=0.2569, c3=0.1149, c4=-0.03038. The sin(c1+c2*t) with c1=0 gives sin(c2*t). This matches GT exactly.

Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 21: P*c0*sin(c1 + c2*t) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5**

Same as Candidate 16 plus a constant c5. Set c5=0. Match.

**Candidate 27: P*c0*sin(c1+c2*t) + P*c3 + P*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6**

Set c3=0, c6=0, and same as before. Match.
